4.8           In its present financial condition, DMEU is unable to provide for appropriate
maintenance of the system and cannot accumulate the funds necessary for replacement of urgently
needed equipment. Nor is it in a position to cover debt service, improved maintenance and increased
chemical costs needed to properly treat wastewater without increases in user charges and improvement
in collections.
4.9           Due to the general negative economic environment, the city has witnessed a decline in
local industrial output through closures and operations at low capacity, and a net outward migration of
the population. This has led to shrinkages in water demand. Over the last two years, billed water
sales went down by 12% (10%  in 1994) for domestic consumers; 32% (13% in 1994) for non-
domestic consumers; and 19 % (I I% in 1994) for all consumer categories. Combined average tariff
per m3 of water sold increased by 51 % in 1994, slightly below the 55 % increase in operating costs.
A faster decline in non-domestic consumption is accentuated in terms of overall revenue as the
domestic consumer is subsidized through cross subsidies. Non-domestic water consumption, as a
percentage of total consumption, has declined from 31% in 1992 to 26% in 1994. Thus fixed costs
have to be recovered from a declining sales base.
C. Tariff Levels, Subsidies and Transfers
4.10          Riga Urban Transport. Ticketing for the three municipal public transport companies
is unified and a single fare is established by the City Council. Although there was previously a zone
system in effect, this was eliminated in July 1994 by the newly elected city administration. At
present, a single fare of 8 santimes is charged for all distances. This fare was introduced in March



- 26 -
1995 and represents a one-third increase over the previous fare or roughly equivalent to the rate of
inflation. Further increases are being discussed in case of a rise in electricity charges.
4.11           The price of a monthly pass valid for 7 days per week is Ls. 3.50 for an adult. This
amounts to only 35 % of the estimated price of an equivalent number of single tickets (Ls. 10 per
month). The estimated discount is 65 %. Such monthly ticket sales amount to 43 % of total revenues
and cover more than 70% of total passenger rides. An approach to the rationalization of
concessionary fares was agreed with the municipality during the appraisal and will be implemented
upon completion of the transport model now under preparation.
4.12           Monthly ticket prices are further discounted for a number of classes of passengers.
Schoolchildren pay only 22% of the cost of an adult pass. Pensioners pay only 39% of the cost of an
adult pass and pensioners over seventy years of age pay only 19%. Former political prisoners and
children under seven travel for free. Concessionary fares for schoolchildren, small children and
former political prisoners are required under state law. Concessionary fares for pensioners are not a
state requirement and have been adopted independently by the municipality. As noted above, the
public transport enterprises are not compensated for carrying passengers at reduced fares. The total
cost of the concessionary fares program is estimated to be Ls. 1.6 million. The municipality
compensates the municipal public transport enterprises for uncovered losses excluding depreciation.
This subsidy amounted to Ls. 3 million for 1994 or Ls. 1.4 million in net subsidy over and above the
level required to cover concessionary fares. This represents a subsidy level of approximately 15%
which is considered to be justifiable considering the positive externalities associated with public
transport including reduced congestion and decreased expenditure on roads and road maintenance.
This compares favorably with other countries in the Region such as Russia where a reduction in
subsidies to 50% of cost recovery fares is targeted.

4.13          Daugavpils Water and Wastewater. In accordance with agreements reached with the
City of Daugavpils and DMEU, tariffs for household and institutional customers were increased on
October 1, 1995, by approximately 80% to 12.5 santimes per m3 for water and wastewater services.
Industrial customers continue to pay 9 santimes for water and 6.6 santimes for wastewater for a
combined charge of 15.6 santimes per m3. This was the first increase since June 1, 1994, and will be
sufficient to cover current operating costs including payment of taxes and provision for maintenance.
This should improve the financial status of DMEU considerably and allow for resumption of various
treatment processes which were discontinued due to lack of funds.
D. Ticketing, Billing and Collection
4.14          Riga Urban Transport. Bus and tram tickets are sold mostly through third parties
such as news agents' kiosks and post offices, and by bus and tram drivers. Monthly concessionary
tickets are sold at TTP head office, and in addition, at post offices for pensioners. Sales commissions
of up to 5% are paid to third parties, whereas drivers get 10% commission, paid with their salaries.
Tickets are distributed by TTP and all cash collected, except for sales by drivers, is handled by TTP.
Ticket revenue is allocated amongst the three companies on the basis of seat/kilometers operated by
each company, irrespective of actual passengers carried. Based on seat/kilometers reported by each
company every month, TTP distributes the revenue and transfers the cash due, net of commissions, to
Imanta and Talava. TTP makes a monthly advance payment by the tenth day, and final settlement by
the twenty fifth day of the following month. Talava's Inter-city bus ticket sales are controlled by it
directly.
4.15          The present system of ticket revenue distribution is inequitable and leads to inefficient
practices. Revenue is determined by numbers of seats and distances travelled, with no regard to
numbers of passengers carried. The transport companies operate as many seat/kilometers as they can
without direct reference to customer demand.
4.16          As agreed with the city council, service contracts between the city council and the
transport companies, as required under this project and referred to below, will provide for new
revenue collection and distribution procedures. The city council, through its Public Transport Unit
(PTU), will be responsible for ticket revenue collection, including the issue of tickets and passes.
Any revenue collected by the transport companies will be handed over to PTU on the day of
collection. Ticket revenue will be distributed on the basis of number of passengers and distance
carried (passenger/kilometers). Transport operators will be permitted under the contract to operate an
incentive scheme to reward management and staff for good performance. The terms of the scheme
and the payments will be subject to the approval of the city council.
4.17          Daugavpils Water and Wastewater. Two different computerized billing systems
operate for metered and non metered consumers. About 94% of domestic consumers (38,000 in total)
are not metered, whereas the majority of non domestic consumers (800 in total) are metered. Non
metered consumers are billed on the basis of notional consumption according to set standard
consumption rates per person or business. Non metered consumers are not issued with monthly bills
as these are fixed. The consumer is notified of any changes which may occur, such as increase in
tariff, change in numbers in the household. All communication, such as notification of revised bills,
reminders of overdue accounts, paying-in-books, are hand delivered by the enterprise staff. Metered
consumers are billed monthly on the basis of readings taken by meter readers of the enterprise.



- 28 -
Metered bills are either hand delivered by meter readers or posted. Domestic consumers pay their
bills mostly through banks or post offices by means of standard pre-printed paying-in-books.
4.18          Metering of apartment blocks has been identified as a key priority for basic water
demand management and conservation. Although installation of block meters started in the middle of
1993, progress has been extremely slow due to lack of available resources. Funding has been
allocated under the project for the installation of meters in each apartment block building.
4.19          The present billing system needs to be upgraded so as to provide accurate, reliable
and timely management information and accounting data. The twinning arrangement under the
project with the water utility of Tampere, Finland, is expected to provide assistance in this regard.
4.20          Poor collection performance has been a major source of financial hardship for the
enterprise. The situation has progressively become worse and uncollected bills now represent over
four months' annual billing. The major difficulty is with industrial consumers who account for 62%
of uncollected bills (237 days of billing), followed by municipal enterprises (121 days), and domestic
consumers (61 days). Bad debts at present are estimated at Ls. 300,000. The future levels of bad
debts will be gradually brought down against set targets: 15% for 1996, 10% for 1997 to 1999,
7.5% for 2000, and 5% thereafter. It was also agreed with DMEU that consumer receivables, net
of bad debts, will not exceed 60 days' annual billing from end 1996 onwards and that the
municipality will allow DMEU to undertake disconnection of customers and other actions as
necessary to achieve this ratio. [para 6.1(i)].
E. Future Financial Performance
4.21          In all cases, there is need for substantial improvement in financial performance of the
municipal enterprises involved in the project. In particular, there is a need for improvement on direct
and indirect cost recovery as necessary to improve key financial ratios, to maintain appropriate debt
service coverage and to provide for adequate maintenance and future investment.  Each of the
enterprises will be required to maintain user charges and transfers sufficient to maintain: debt
service coverage of 1.3 times, positive net income and appropriate return on assets. Detailed
financial projections have been prepared for existing enterprises and special issues and conditions are
summarized below. (See also Annex C).
4.22          Riga Urban Transport. Financial projections prepared during the development of
detailed business plans for Imanta, Talava and the Tram and Trolleybus Park suggest that financial
performance can improve to desired levels provided that: (i) the municipality maintain the current
level of subsidy indefinitely; (ii) the municipality compensate municipal public transport operators for
carrying passengers at concessionary fares; (iii) a mechanism for increasing real fares and transfers to
cost recovery levels; and (iv) improved revenue controls and inspection are instituted that would
reduce fare evasion 50% by increasing the number of inspectors and increasing the amount of fines.
In addition, revenue will be increased and operating costs reduced through the project itself as it will
allow for the acquisition of new vehicles, retirement of the more dilapidated vehicles, provision for
adequate maintenance of vehicle fleet, and technical support and training.
4.23          The City of Riga will be required to maintain user charges and transfers
sufficient to enable the three public transport companies to achieve: debt-service coverage of
1.3 times, positive net income and a return on net assets of 10% from 1997 onwards. [para



- 29 -
6.1(j)]. The Riga City Council has agreed to an annual 5 % real increase in fares over the project
period over and above inflation and increases in input costs and taxes. The Riga City Council has
also agreed to compensate the transport companies for losses due to carrying passengers at
concessionary fares. The precise mechanism for determining such compensation will have to be
developed; however, preliminary estimates suggest that this will require approximately Ls. 1.6 million
per year out of the municipal budget or approximately 2.6% of total city revenues for 1995.
Increased costs of inspection are expected to be defrayed by increased fines.
4.24          If these conditions are adopted it is expected that cash flow generated will not only be
sufficient to cover the costs of debt service but would also allow for an adequate ongoing program of
fleet renewal within three to four years. The companies will thus be in a position to bring down and
maintain the average age of the fleet to the generally accepted norms within the medium term. In the
long term, a balance will need to be achieved between the levels of investments and payment of
dividends to shareholders. The financial projections have assumed no dividend payments.
4.25          Daugavpils Water and Wastewater. Recent tariff increases will enable DMEU to
meet current operating expenses. However, further tariff increases would need to be implemented
over the next five years to raise combined tariffs for all customers to 23.4 santimes per m3 of water
sold (estimated in 1995 prices), excluding 18% VAT, to cover increased operating costs as required
to adequately maintain equipment, achieve financial viability and meet the proposed financial targets
set under the project. The schedule for these increases is summarized in Table 4.4. In addition to
the required 1.3 times debt service coverage, the utility would be expected to achieve a positive
net income and a minimum annual return on net assets of 1.5% from 1997 onwards. [para 6.1
(k)].

4.27         These tariff increases have been calculated assuming substantial donor contributions
towards the construction of the wastewater collection and treatment facilities, and including cost
savings due to phase out of surface water treatment. The tariff increases also allow for: (a) write-off
of existing bad debts and repayment in equal installments of existing backlog of unpaid taxes due to
the municipality over the next five years; (b) future levels of bad debts as noted above; (c) consumer
receivables, after bad debts not exceeding 60 days' annual billing from end 1996 onwards; (d) staff
reduction (through attrition) of 5% in 1996 and 5% in 1997; (e) annual payroll increases of 3% in
real terms to allow for recruitment of new staff, and for motivation and retention of staff; and (f)
adjustments of norms for household water consumption to actual measured levels by completion of
block and bulk metering program by 1998.
4.28          With these tariff increases, DMEU would be able to substantially improve key
financial performance ratios including appropriate debt service coverage, positive cash flow and
improved maintenance practices. From 2000 onwards, the utility will also be in a position to finance,
from internally generated funds, an ongoing capital investment program of rehabilitation of the main
water network over a long term period.
F. Affordability
4.29          An assessment of the affordability of the user charge increases discussed above for
each of the investment programs has been made and suggests that the resulting charges are, in all
cases, reasonable and affordable and will not require any modification to existing social support
programs. As user charge increases will be necessary for all services including those not involved in
the present project, affordability has been evaluated by comparison of share of household expenditure
on affected services as compared to international averages.
4.30          Riga Urban Transport. Monthly ticket prices of Ls. 3.5 for adults represent only 4%
of the current monthly wage. (The national average wage is Ls. 85 per month. Though Riga wages
are known to be higher, no recent information is available on wage data for the city so the national
average is used as a conservative estimate.) Concessionary monthly fares for pensioners of Ls. 1.35
amount to only 4.5% of the average pensioner's income. Annual fare increases of 5% in real terms
will result in a 48% cumulative increase by the end of 8 years. At that point, monthly fares would



- 31 -
still amount to only about 6% of monthly wages. Furthermore, it can be expected that real wages
would also have increased. This compares to a norm of 10% in most other middle income countries.4
4.31          Daugavpils Water and Wastewater. User charges in Daugavpils have until recently
been quite low in comparison with those in other cities. Riga has a combined charge of 17 santimes
per m3 of water for households and 25 santimes per m3 for industry. In Liepaja, the combined
household charge is 11 santimes and 28 santimes for industry. The recent increase in household user
charges from 7 to 12.5 santimes is appropriate and brings tariff levels in Daugavpils to a level
comparable with other Latvian cities. Further increases to 23.4 santimes over a five year period
would be necessary to support increased costs associated with improved wastewater treatment and
increased depreciation charges due to the new investments. (All tariff levels are quoted in 1995
constant terms).
4.32          The recently adopted tariff amounts to 95 santimes per person per month based on
average billed consumption of 250 liters per day. With an average household size of 2.4, this
amounts to Ls. 2.28 per family per month or approximately 1.9% of household income (estimated for
Daugavpils as 117 lats per month on average). This compares to a norm of 3 to 5 percent used to
evaluate the affordability of other water sector projects. Even after full phase-in of all tariff increases
necessary to finance the project and increase in the billed quantities to actual consumption levels, total
expenditure on water and wastewater would amount to Ls. 4.78 per household per month or roughly
4.1 % of household income. This is estimated conservatively and does not include any assumption of
an increase in per capita income over the period. (This does not include VAT, as charges for
municipal services are exempted as of November 1995).
G. Organizational Issues
4.33          Municipal enterprises already enjoy a substantial degree of autonomy and are run as
separate budgetary entities by independent enterprise directors appointed by the respective city
council. Increased autonomy would be achieved under the project by strengthening of contractual
arrangements between the municipality and the municipal enterprises, encouragement of movement
towards full incorporation as a joint stock company in combination with suitable contractual and
regulatory arrangements deemed necessary to protect the public interest, and by improvement of the
basis for determination of tariff levels. Introduction of these measures should ensure that municipal
enterprises involved in the project have sufficient resources to maintain new equipment and facilities
and appropriate incentives to increase operational efficiency.
4.34          It should be noted, however, that most municipal enterprises are afflicted with
substantial operational inefficiencies. Overstaffing is a problem at all levels and departments and is
exacerbated by management practices. Financial accounting systems are inefficient, antiquated and do
not provide appropriate management information. Maintenance and operations protocols are poor.
Despite substantial management autonomy, little has been done to address these problems and
technical assistance will be required to allow for exposure to new management techniques and
approaches.
4Armstrong-Wright, Alan and Thiriez, Sebastion, Bus Services: Reducing Costs, Raising Standards,
(Washington, DC: World Bank Technical Paper Number 68, Urban Transport Series, 1987), p. 68.



- 32 -
4.35          Specific measures proposed to address these problems are detailed below.
4.36          Riga Urban Transport. Draft contracts between the municipality and the three public
transport enterprises have been prepared. These establish the terms and conditions for service
delivery and the rights and responsibilities of the enterprises relative to the municipality and vice
versa. The contracts will provide guidelines for determination of fares and will establish a
mechanism to provide for compensation for concessionary fares. The city has presented a proposal
for the rationalization of fares during the appraisal and this will be implemented by the PTU.
Adoption of satisfactory contractual arrangements will be required as a condition of
effectiveness. [para 6.3(c)] Movement towards incorporation of the three companies is being
discussed; however, it has so far been rejected by the municipality given that most of the benefits of
joint stock company status already apply to municipal enterprises.
4.37          Detailed business plans have been developed with the assistance of consultants
financed under the Japanese Grant and have been agreed with the three public transport enterprises.
Key points of the business plans are as follows:
(a) The staff to vehicle ratio should be reduced by at least 10% over the next several years. This
can be easily implemented through attrition.
(b) Improved revenue, costing and inventory control systems should be implemented as necessary
to improve efficiency and effectiveness of administrative staff. Adoption of a revenue,
costing and inventory control system acceptable to the Bank will be required by June 1,
1996. [para 6.1(1)]
(c) Funding for piloting of ticketing systems is included under the project and will be evaluated as
a measure to decrease fare evasion as well as to collect information necessary for
rationalization of routing structure.
4.38          Daugavpils Water and Wastewater. It has been agreed with the municipality during
appraisal that the contract and enterprise statutes for DMEU would be revised to formalize the
relationship between the utility and the municipality. Conclusion of a contract between the City of
Daugavpils and DMEU will be required as a condition of effectiveness. [para 6.3(d)] A key issue
to be addressed in the contract is the establishment of a formal mechanism for determination of user
charges. It is also being proposed that the enterprise be incorporated as a joint stock company
wholly owned by the municipality. Further analysis of this issue will be one of the elements of the
twinning arrangement. Daugavpils will be required to present a reorganization plan for DMEU
by January 1, 1997, and undertake its implementation by December 31, 1997. [para 6. l(m)].
4.39          The situation regarding overstaffing at the enterprise has been discussed, and the
municipality has agreed in principle to separation of the internal plumbing maintenance unit from
DMEU which will reduce headcount by approximately 10 percent. Further reductions of 10% over
the next two years are assumed in the financial projections and can be achieved easily through
attrition. Other organizational weaknesses in finance and operations will be addressed through the
twinning arrangement with the water utility of Tampere, Finland.



- 33 -
V. PROJECT BENEFITS AND RISKS
A. Project Benefits
5.1           The project supports the development of municipal infrastructure identified as a
priority by the Government of Latvia in its Public Investment Program and by the World Bank in its
CAS. The project will provide for a number of critically needed investments for priority sub-projects
identified by the state and local governments with the assistance of the World Bank and donors during
project preparation. The project will also support the implementation of a number of necessary
financial, operational and regulatory reforms needed to ensure the sustainability of the proposed
investment program and to allow for the future development of the municipal sector. Implementation
of agreed policy measures and further conditions under discussion will lead to increased commercial
viability of the enterprises participating in the project and will form the basis for potential increased
private sector involvement in municipal services in the future. Improvement of the financial condition
of municipal services enterprises and increased movement towards cost recovery will also limit
demands on local government resources. The project supports the government's efforts towards
decentralization by providing local governments with a source of investment funding for priority
projects.
5.2           Specific benefits of sub-projects are noted below. A discussion of assumptions and
calculations is contained in Annex F.
5.3           Riga Urban Transport. The purchase of new articulated buses and trolleybuses, and
the disposal of the oldest buses and trolleybuses, will improve the overall performance of the public
transport fleets and will prevent the continued deterioration that would occur without the project.
This, together with the supply of spares and improvements to trains, will permit maintenance staff
reductions and would effect substantial maintenance cost savings. Improved financial and
management information systems would allow for reduction of administrative staff. This will enable
staff reduction of 10% to be achieved through attrition within two years.
5.4           The estimated economic rate of return is 22 percent. The net present value of the
project is US$8.8 million with an assumed discount rate of 10 percent. Benefits due to reduction in
passenger waiting time have been estimated conservatively given the partial nature of the
rehabilitation effort and represent a small portion (5%) of total benefits. The majority of benefits are
due to prevention of fleet deterioration which would otherwise result in increased vehicle operation
costs. These calculations and the underlying assumptions are explained in Annex 5. The sensitivity
of the ERR was measured against project costs and assumed benefits. It is possible to maintain an
ERR of 12% with an assumed increase in project costs of 38% and an assumed decrease in benefits of
28%.
5.5           Daugavpils Water and Wastewater. Construction of a new groundwater wellfield will
enable diversification of water supplies and development of the basis for complete movement away
from surface water. Daugavpils is downstream from major chemical factories and there have been
several accidents involving accidental discharge of toxic chemicals into the river. (Several years ago
cyanide was discharged into the water and required cutting off all surface water intakes).
Diversification of water supplies will minimize the social cost of such temporary pollution incidents.
Eventual complete transition from surface water will substantially reduce the public health risks from
undetected spills. It is not possible to fully quantify the benefits of the proposed investment,



- 34 -
although it can be reasonably assumed that they would be significant given the positive impact on
public health and environment. A least cost analysis was conducted using the alternative of upgrading
the surface water treatment works to include carbon filters and ozonation. Estimated costs of full
wellfield development were equivalent to construction of the new groundwater intake, though
operating costs for water treatment would be 25% higher due to chemicals costs. Although this
alternative would result in a reduction of THMs and improved water quality, it would still leave water
supplies vulnerable to sudden or undetected contamination.
5.6           The measures to be instituted in rehabilitation of the wastewater treatment works
would significantly reduce the current discharge of BOD and Nitrogen. The proposed project
supports the commitments of the Government of Latvia, as party to the Helsinki agreements, to fulfill
the recommendations of the Baltic Sea Joint Comprehensive Environmental Action Program by
reducing pollution of the Baltic Sea from a priority "hot spot". As with the water supply component,
the benefits of improved wastewater treatment are difficult to quantify. A least cost analysis was
conducted and included evaluation of simple biological treatment, biofiltration and full biological
treatment at a new site. Simple biological treatment was selected as the most cost effective solution.
5.7           Municipal Development Fund. Sub-projects to be financed under the MDF will be
identified only during project implementation. A criteria for selection of sub-projects for financing
under the MDF is that they achieve a minimum economic rate of return of 12%.
B. Project Risks
5.8           The major risks are that: (i) participating municipalities would not adhere to agreed
policy conditionality and/or financial and performance covenants including provision of counterpart
financing; (ii) inability of local governments to manage project implementation leading to construction
and procurement delays; (iii) inability of local governments to prepare satisfactory investment
proposals for financing under the MDF; and (iv) inadequate supervision of MDF projects.
5.9           These risks will be mitigated by: (i) prior agreement with municipalities on terms and
conditions required for sub-loan effectiveness and, in particular, related to financial covenants,
organizational arrangements and local counterpart financing; (ii) requirement that sub-loan agreements
between the participating municipalities and the Ministry of Finance on behalf of the Government of
Latvia enable the Ministry of Finance to deduct interest and principal repayments from taxes and
other revenues collected on behalf of local governments by the state tax administration; (iii) provision
of technical assistance for critical areas of project implementation; (iv) adequate staffing of the PMUs
for the three primary sub-projects; (v) addition of consultant staff to the PIP unit to assist with
administration of the MDF and to support municipalities in preparation and supervision of projects;
and (vi) establishment of a central Project Coordination Unit (PCU) to monitor compliance with loan
and sub-loan covenants and with project implementation timetable.



- 35 -
VI. AGREEMENTS
6.1    The following agreements were reached during Negotiations:
(a) The City of Riga will implement all measures outlined in the Public Transport Policy
Statement of July 11, 1995, including payment of compensation due to the public transport
companies in connection with concessionary fares that may be required by the City of Riga.
(para 2.20)
(b) Projects to be financed under the MDF will be selected in accordance with criteria agreed
with the Bank. (para 2.31)
(c) DMEU will take all measures necessary to comply with the environmental requirements of an
environmental monitoring plan to be agreed with the Bank. (para 2.56)
(d) The City of Riga will cause the RBMST to monitor public transport emissions in accordance
with a monitoring plan agreed with the Bank. (para 2.57)
(e) The City of Riga will maintain the PTU with functions and responsibilities acceptable to the
Bank and with staff in adequate numbers, with qualifications, experience and terms of
reference satisfactory to the Bank. (para 3.1(a))
(f)  DMEU will maintain the PMU with functions and responsibilities acceptable to the Bank and
with staff in adequate numbers, with qualifications, experience and terms of reference
satisfactory to the Bank. (para 3.1(b))
(g) The Government of Latvia will maintain the PCU with functions and responsibilities
acceptable to the Bank and with staff in adequate numbers with qualifications, experience and
terms of reference satisfactory to the Bank. (para 3.1(d))
(h) A mid-term review by the Bank will take place no later than September 30, 1998. (para 3.3)
(i) DMEU will take such actions as are necessary to ensure that consumer receivables, net of bad
debts, will not exceed 60 days' annual billing from the end of 1996 onwards and the City of
Daugavpils will allow DMEU to undertake disconnection of customers and other actions as
necessary to achieve this ratio. (para 4.20)
(j) The City of Riga will be required to maintain user charges and transfers sufficient to enable
the three public transport companies to achieve: debt service coverage of 1.3 times, positive
net income and a return on net assets of 10% from 1997 onwards. (para 4.23)
(k) The City of Daugavpils and DMEU will take such actions as are necessary to enable DMEU
to achieve: debt service coverage of 1.3 times, positive net income and a return on net assets
of 1.5 % from 1997 onwards. (para 4.25)
(I) The three Riga transport companies will adopt a revenue, costing and inventory control
system acceptable to the Bank by June 1, 1996. (para 4.37(b))



- 36 -
(m) The City of Daugavpils will be required to present a reorganization plan for DMEU by
January 1, 1997 and undertake its implementation by December 31, 1997. (para 4.38)
6.2    The following action has been taken by the Borrower as a condition of Board presentation:
The Municipal Development Fund was established by Decree of the Cabinet of Ministers on
November 10, 1995. (para 2.30)
6.3    The following actions will be required as a condition of effectiveness:
(a) Execution of the subsidiary loan agreement between the City of Riga and the Ministry of
Finance. (para 2.35)
(b) Execution of the subsidiary loan agreement between the DMEU and the Ministry of Finance
with the guarantee of the City of Daugavpils. (para 2.35)
(c) Adoption of satisfactory contractual arrangements between the City of Riga and the three
public transport companies. (para 4.36)
(d) Conclusion of a contract, satisfactory to the Bank, between the City of Daugavpils and
DMEU for the provision of water and wastewater services. (para 4.38)
6.4    The following will be required as a condition of disbursement for the Daugavpils Water and
Wastewater component of the Project:
All conditions for NEFCO co-financing and for grant financing by the Governments of
Sweden, Denmark, Finland and EU PHARE will be met. (para 2.38)
Recommendation
6.5    Subject to the above, the Project is suitable for a Bank Loan of US$27.3 million equivalent at
the standard variable interest rate with a maturity of 17 years including 4 years of grace.

RiGAS DOMNE                                                 PJGACT\'COUNCI
Latvia: Municipal -Services Development Project
Riga Urban Transport
Policy Statement of the Riga City Council
on Public Transport in Riga
General
The policy of Riga City Council is to reform public transport and create market
conditions in order to improve service levels, efficiency and financial viability. it
intends to move tariffs closer to cost recovery levels, to stabilise subsidies and to
eliminate uncovered costs.. Competition will be introduced and the private sector
encouraged to participate in the provision of public transport.
The existing public transport enterprises will be required to implement agreed
business plans and to enter into contracts with the Municipality for the supply of
services.
An appropriate regulatory authority (Riga City Public Transport Unit) willbe set up
in the Transport and Communications Board to oversee public transport operators
and the ticketing system.
Tariffs
Public transport tariffs will be increased by 5% in real terms (i.e. over and above
inflation) each year until an acceptable level of financial viability is reached. Also,
the tariff structure will be rationalised in order to relate tai.ffs more closely to
distance travelled and costs, and to improve weekly and monthly passes.
Concessionary travel
The City Council intends to implement proposals to compensate operators for
providing concessionary travel. The amount of compensation will be related to the
differernce between the futl fare and the concessionary amount paid. Since the
concessions are to meet social needs the compensation will be funded from the
Social Budget.
Revenue Control Inspectors
In order to reduce the very substantial amount of tariff evasion on public transport,
the City Council intends to set up within the Municipallty a Public Transport
Revenue Control Service that will function according to the principle of self-
financing, basing on the contract between the Control Service and public transport
companies. The number of revenue control inspectors will be gradually increased.
Riga City Council will promote the increase of the fine for tariff evasion in order to
retain an appropriate deterrent. (The present fine is 0.50 Ls).



* ANNEX A
Page 2 of 3
Riga City Public Transport Unit
The Riga City Council will establish an ef'ective Public Transport Unit (PTU) within
the Transport and Comnunications Board. The functions of the PTU are to:
(a) develop, oversee, monitor, and coordinate public transport services;
(b) draw up contracts with public transport operators regarding levels of
service, routes, tariffs, subsidies and concessionary travel compensation;
(c) oversee the tariffs and ticketing system, including the gathering and
distribution of revenue, and the revenue inspection teams;
(d) develop and administer a public transport vehicle and operator licensing
system;
(e) oversee the implementation of the public transport component of the
project funded by the World Bank.
The PTU will be provided with adequate staff, taking into account the proposals of
the World Bank experts, in order to undertake these functions effectively.
Municipal Public Transport Enterprises
The Riga City Council intends that the municipal public transport enterprises will
follow sound commercial practices. This will involve each enterprise having a
board of director, separate accounts and detailed costing and revenue accounting
system. The management of each enterprise will be answerable to its board of
director, and will act within the framework of the agreed business plan. The
management and staff will receive appropriate incentives for good performance.
The enterprises will enter into contracts with the Municipality for the supply of
services which will be overseen by the PTU, as above. Each board of directors will
include a representative of the Municipality.
To increase efficiency, it is intended that the contract system will encourage the
Municipal public transport enterprises to compete amongst themselves for routes.
Also the enterprises will not be protected from any healthy competition from the
private sector should this arise.
The aim is that the Municipal public transport enterprises will gradually improve
their economic activities that could stirnulate the at-raction of the local and foreign
investments.
Implementation of Actiom Plans
In order to reap the full benefits of the World Bank loan, the Riga City Council will
ensure that the bodies concerned (i.e. the Municipality, IMAANTA, TALAVA, and
TTP) effectively implement all the Action Plans set out in the agreed Business
Plans For Public Transport Enterprises.
Participation of the Private Sector
The policy of the Riga City Council is to promote efficient competition and to
encourage the participation of the private sector in the provision of public
transport services. The City will perrnit private operators to operate public
transport services provided that the vehicles meet safety and environmental
standards and the operator can demonstrate evidence of professional competence.
Also, PTU may issue contracts to private operators for the provision of required
services, and to permit them to take part, as appropriate, in the ticketing system
and concessionary travel compensation scheme.



ANNEX A
Page 3 of 3
To encourage private investment in public transport, and to improve the
opportunities of the private sector to obtain funding, private operators will be
provided with an appropriate regulatory and legal environment.
Non-rnotorised transport
In view of the very considerable economic and environmental benefits of non-
motorised transport, the Riga City Council intends to promote greater use of non-
rnotorised modes (cycling and walking). The opportunities will be exarnined and a
programme developed for the provision of facilities for cyclists and pedestrians
together with appropriate publicity.
O.Batarevskis
Deputy Chairman
Riga City Council






ANNEX B

REPUBLIC OF LATVIA, MINISTRY OF ECONOMY
GUIDELINES FOR SUBMISSION OF PROJECTS
TO THE MUNICIPAL DEVELOPMENT FUND
THE PUBLIC INVESTMENT PROGRAM DEPARTMENT
DRAFT - JULY 4, 1995
Abbreviations and Acronyms:
CBA -Cost benefit analysis
CEA -Cost Effectiveness Analysis
BCR -Benefit Cost Ratio
GoL -Government of Latvia
IRR -Internal Rate of Return
MDF-Municipal Development Fund
NPV -Net Present Value
PIP -Public Investment Program
PIPD -Public Investment Program Department
MoF -Ministry of Finance
MoE -Ministry of Economy
1. Introduction
1.1    The Municipal Development Fund (MDF) is administered by the Public Investment Program
Department (PIPD) of the Ministry of Economy (MoE). These guidelines are issued by the
Department in order to regulate submission of projects for financing from the MDF. They state
requirements and procedures of submission of projects with which applicants must comply.
2. Objective of the MDF
2.1    The main objective of the MDF is to mobilize resources from private lenders, central
government, donor agencies, and local governments themselves and make them available for
municipalities for investment in urban infrastructure. Thus the MDF is an additional source of funds
for the municipalities to finance projects being under their responsibility described in the law "On the
municipalities." Other objectives include strengthening the operational capacity and efficiency of local
governments by assisting them in the design, appraisal, and execution of investment programs;
rationalizing programs moving away from the ad hoc investment practices; and injecting rational
criteria into the geographical and sectoral distribution of funds.
2.2    The MDF is particularly well suited to the needs of smaller cities, which may lack
administrative skills and access to capital markets.
2.3    The Fund commences its activity with an initial capital of 3.5 million USD loan from the
World Bank. Financing from the state budget and other sources is foreseen also at the later stage. The
loan is made to the Government of Latvia (GoL) and will be on-lent to participating municipalities to
implement the proposed sub-projects. The funds can in turn be lent by the municipalities to the
concerned municipal enterprises. In some circumstances it is possible to lend directly to the
municipal enterprise upon obtaining a suitable guarantee from the municipality. In both cases, the



ANNEX B
Page 2 of 10
municipality is responsible for repayment of the sub-loan in case of default by the municipal
enterprise.
3. Supervisory bodies of the MDF
3.1    The Fund is governed by the Board of the MDF approved by the Cabinet of Ministers. The
Board consists of one representative from Ministry of Economy, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of
Environmental Protection and Regional Development and the Union of Local Governments. The
Board approves financing of projects from the MDF. During the Board approval session a
representative from the corresponding sector ministry shall be present (with voting right).
4. Projects eligible under financing from the MDF
4.1    Only investment projects in the area of municipal services meeting assessed needs and
reflecting both of the local communities' and national priorities. Those project by sector are:
(a)    Energy:
(i)    rehabilitation and construction of heating supply systems and boiler houses;
(ii)   rehabilitation and construction of gas supply networks; energy saving by
introduction of metering of consumption of heating, gas and water;
(iii)   reduction of energy losses by insulation of municipally owned apartment
houses and other public buildings.
(b)    Transportation:
(i)    rehabilitation and construction of streets, roads, bridges;
(ii)   introduction of traffic solutions aiming at improvement of transport conditions;
(iii)   rehabilitation and construction of infrastructure used by transportation
enterprises.
(c)    Environment:
(i)    water supply and waste water treatment facilities;
(ii)   solid waste disposal and processing;
(iii)   rehabilitation and construction of dams and common use melioration objects.
(d)    Education - rehabilitation and construction of schools;
(e)    Health care:
(i)    rehabilitation and construction of health care facilities;
(ii)    purchase of medical equipment.
(f')    Social care - rehabilitation and construction of different type facilities for retired,
handicapped and orphans;
(g)    Rehabilitation and construction of premises for municipal police and other public
buildings for social, cultural or administrative needs of the local community.



ANNEX B
Page 3 of 10
5. Servicing fee
5.1    To cover operational expenses of the MDF a service fee shall be added to the interest rate of
the loan. This fee shall cover costs and salaries of specialists hired by the MDF for project appraisal
(civil construction engineer, a project economist). Procurement and disbursement will be the
responsibility of the MoF, and the work of the members of the Board corresponding to their input.
6. Project appraisal criteria
6.1   Submitted projects should be subjected to cost benefit analysis or should have a business plan.
Alternatives should be adequately assessed and the least cost solution (investment plus recurrent
costs). Projects should meet existing technical, construction and environmental standards and
regulations;
6.2   The economic rate of return should be demonstrated to be over 12%;
6.3   For revenue generating sectors the financial feasibility of proposed investments should be
made and a plan for cost recovery (including proper maintenance) provided. Financial projections
should be made including income statements, balance sheets and cash flows of the project owner. A
minimum debt service coverage of 1.3 should be maintained by the enterprise or department
implementing the project. Minimum cost recovery targets should be set by the sector. If tariff
increases for municipal services are necessary to meet these targets, then this should be formally
agreed with the Council of the municipality and the agreement submitted prior to approval of
sub-project;
6.4   Borrowers should demonstrate their existing financial, technical and administrative capability
to operate and maintain the proposed services. Borrowers should demonstrate also adequate project
management capacity to design and supervise project implementation and control project costs.
Where necessary, borrowers should be required to take necessary steps to improve their capability in
these areas, or to restructure the public utilities enterprises to meet the requirements;
6.5   Environmental impact analysis (EIA) of proposed investments should be made and necessary
mitigation measures built into project according to the Latvian law on environment protection and
rules of the World Bank;
6.6   During the first cycle the participation of the MDF in financing should not exceed the amount
of 500,000 Ls and the share of the MDF can not exceed 80% of the total project costs. At least 10%
of the cost of the project has to be covered by the borrowing municipality;
6.7   The MDF can participate in financing only of those projects which exceed 20-30% of the total
budget of the borrowing municipality and which could not reasonably be financed by the municipality
on its own within 34 years. Debt servicing payments may not exceed 15% of the yearly budget of
the borrowing municipality in cost recovering sectors or 7-10% if the credit is repaid by the
municipal budget;
6.8   MDF credits for sectors covered by special budgets such as Road Fund, Environment
Protection Fund etc., can be issued only if at least 20% of corresponding municipal special budget is
allocated for this project.



ANNEX B
Page 4 of 10
Box 1. The Project Concept Paper
The Project Concept Paper (PCP) should be used to seek out the views of the Government and
other stakeholders at an early stage of the project cycle. The paper should specific the objectives of the
proposed project, the problem it intends to address, the alternative ways of addressing the problems, the
potential benefits/costs and the intended beneficiaries and potential losers. It shall be submitted at the
standard Form (see Annex A)
7. Terms of loans
7.1    The loans for the MDF will be given for up to 17 years depending on the nature of the
investment and corresponding to the benefit stream of the investment. Repayment has to be started
after completing the construction but not later than after 1/4 of the whole loan period.
7.2    Funds disbursement from proceeds of the World Bank loan must satisfy World Bark
procurement procedures. For projects below 25,000 Ls local shopping shall be applied. For civil
construction works between 25,000 and 150,000 Ls, national shopping will apply. For goods
contracts between 25.000 and 150,000 Ls international shopping will apply. International competitive
bidding (ICB) will be used for all contracts over 150,000 Ls. All ICB contracts will require prior
review by the Bank.
7.3    The World Bank would review the first 3 projects on no objection basis and any individual
project larger than 250.000 Ls.
7.4    Funds on-lent from proceeds of the World Bank could, with the approval of the MoF, be
recycled.
8. Project submission procedure
8.1    To receive financing from the MDF municipal projects must be included into
the PIP. Thus the submission cycle is similar to the process of submission of the other PIP projects.
To be included into the PIP all projects must be submitted to the PIPD.
8.2    The project submission cycle begins with the Project Concept Paper (PCP) which shall be
submitted to the PIPD (See Box 1). The PCPs can be submitted throughout the whole year, however
they shall be reviewed four times a year during the first week of the quarter. The idea behind the
PCP is that the applicants should not waste resources on feasibility studies of projects which have no
chance of being included into the PIP. The crucial part of the PCP is the financial information (see
Box 2) about the applicant/enterprise which allows the PIPD to assess his financial viability, technical
and administrative capability to operate and maintain the proposed services. The PCP shall be
approved by the highest elected body of the municipality (Council). An opinion of an appropriate
sector ministry should be supplemented.



ANNEX B
Page 5 of 10
8.3    The paper should be made jointly by applicant, potential source of financing, and discussed
with other stakeholders including potential beneficiaries/affected parties. The final version should be
submitted to the PIPD consideration. In reviewing the PCP, the PIPD examines:
-the consistency of the proposed project with the MDF requirements;
-whether the proposed intervention is consistent with the sectoral and national priorities;
-whether the borrowers can demonstrate financial, technical and administrative capability to
operate and maintain the proposed services.
8.4    On the basis of the recommendations of the PIPD, the MDF Board sends a formal letter to
the sector municipality indicating: (i) formal approval to appraise the project; (ii) a delay of appraisal
pending further discussions of the proposals; or (iii) a rejection of the project. In case of formal
approval to appraise the project, the letter will also specify required issues to be addressed during
appraisal.
8.5    After having received a formal approval from the MDF the applicant can proceed with the
project appraisal. After having completed the appraisal the application shall be submitted to the PIPD.
The project application dossier shall contain:
- the project profile (see Annex B also filled in English);
- the feasibility study;
- opinion of the appropriate sector ministry.
8.6    The PIPD shall screen the project verify/make an financial and economical analysis of the
project and recommend only sound projects to the Board for approval.
8.7    Procurement procedures are to be made by the borrower in cooperation with the MOF.
Payment is made by the MoF.
9. Procedures for projects submission to the PIPD
The process of submission of a project to the PIPD relies on a sequence of the following procedures:
9.1.    Preparation of the Project Concept Paper by the applicant and discussion of the paper with
various stakeholders;
9.2.    Submission of the PCP (on the standard form) to the PIPD for consideration. MDF Board
upon the PIPD recommendation decides what steps should be next, in particular, to appraise or not
appraise. The Board notifies the line ministry giving clearance for appraisal and/or indicates
any other actions that needs to be taken;
9.3.    Project Appraisal. The appraisal report should respond to issues raised by the project
screening criteria in Box 2 and specific issues raised in the Board decision to appraise the project;
9.4.    Preparation of the project feasibility study by the applicant;
9.5.   Submission of the project profile form and PAM to the PIPD for inclusion into the PIP and
financing from the MDF.

PROJECT IMPLEMENTATION PLAN
I. IMPLEMENTATION ARRANGEMENTS
A. Project Implementation Responsibilities
1.    Table A3. 1 summarizes the respective responsibilities of the different implementing and
coordinating agencies involved in the proposed Project and its three component parts.
B. Role of the World Bank During Supervision
2.     The proposed Project would be supervised by Bank personnel from both headquarters and the
Regional Mission for the Baltic Countries. In addition technical specialists from The Swedish Ministry
of Environment, the Finnish Ministry of Environment and the Danish Ministry of Environment,
together with personnel from NEFCO and EU PHARE, would participate in supervision missions.
The proposed supervision plan is summarized in Table A3.2.
3.    Recognizing that the proposed Project would be only the third Bank Project in Latvia
involving large scale construction of civil works and installation of sophisticated mechanical and
electrical equipment, and the first with a component in the cities of Riga and Daugavpils, it is
anticipated that it would require significant supervision. The supervision would concentrate on the
first two years when considerable input would be required for the engineering design and the
procurement aspects of the Riga Urban Transport and the Daugavpils Water and Wastewater
components. In addition, supervision by technical specialists would be required for the respective
project components, as described in the following sections. Savings would be realized by utilizing
staff from the Bank resident mission for project supervision. During the first year of implementation,
a project launch workshop would be organized to provide basic training for the staff of the
implementing agencies in procurement, disbursement, accounting and auditing.
4.    It is anticipated that about 22 staff-weeks of effort for the first two years and about 10 staff-
weeks thereafter would be required for supervision. Following the start-up mission and the project
launch workshop, supervision requirements in the first two years would include two supervision
missions per year to coincide with the production of the semi-annual progress reports by the
respective implementing agencies. In later years, one supervision mission would be conducted each
year, timed to coincide with one of that year's progress reports. The final supervision mission would
be to prepare the Project completion report.
5.    A mid-term review would be conducted to evaluate project progress in general (in terms of
procurement, disbursements, status of construction works and other implementational aspects) and to
assess the status of agreed policy and institutional reforms.

LATVIA MUNICIPAL SERVICES DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
Daugavpils Water Supplv and Wastewater Component
Terms of Reference for the Udensvads Project Management Unit
1.    A project management unit (PMU) is to be formed to coordinate the execution of those
elements of the Municipal Services Development Project related to the Daugavpils water supply and
wastewater component. The PMU will be located at the Daugavpils water and wastewater enterprise
(Udensvads) and will coordinate the aforementioned work throughout the duration of the project.
2.    The duties of the PMU shall include:
2.1    Coordinate, on behalf of Udensvads, the relations between the water enterprise,
Daugavpils Council, the World Bank, NEFCO, the bi-lateral donors, and the
consultants and contractors appointed under the component.
2.2    Monitor the use of the World Bank and the NEFCO loans and the bi-lateral grants.
2.3    On behalf of Udensvads, carry out the following tasks: prepare terms of reference and
letters of invitations for the various consultancies to be carried out under the project;
prepare short-lists of consultants to be invited to submit proposals; prepare technical
specifications and associated bidding documents for the various bidding packages to be
carried out under the project; issue documentation to consultants and contractors,
respond to queries raised, and issue addenda as necessary; evaluate consultants
statements of capability and contractors prequalification documents; evaluate
consultants proposals and contractors bids and prepare evaluation reports; help
Udensvads management with the negotiation and signing of the resulting contracts.
2.4    Coordinate the implementation of recommendations made in World Bank project
supervision reports.
2.5    Prepare semi-annual reports as outlined in Section V of the Project Implementation
Plan and submit to the Project Coordination Unit and to the World Bank.
2.6    Monitor project implementation and expenditure, and prepare and submit
disbursement requests, copies of which should be submitted to the World Bank, the
Project Coordination Unit, and the Ministry of Finance.
2.7    Monitor the training and technology and skill transfer programs to be provided under
the project's technical assistance and twinning arrangements.
2.8    Monitor all aspects of the Daugavpils water supply and wastewater component of the
project and prepare written warnings about possible problems and delays as well as
proposing technical, financial and institutional measures necessary to improve project
implementation.



ANNEX C
Page 6 of 71
2.9    Coordinate the execution of the different contracts to ensure overall work programs
are maintained.
2.10   Monitor the progress of the studies/consultancies commissioned to determine: (i) the
need for any mitigation measures deemed necessary to protect the quality of the
groundwater at the Ziemelu wellfield; and (ii) appropriate alternative methods for the
treatment and reutilization/disposal of the sludge to be generated at the upgraded
wastewater treatment works.
2.11   Hold weekly meetings with Udensvads management to discuss project progress, the
previous week's work program, the coming week's work program, problems
encountered, solutions proposed, performance of consultants and contractors, and any
other important issues.
2.12   Hold regular meetings with Daugavpils City Council to discuss project progress, the
project work program, problems encountered, solutions proposed, performance of
consultants and contractors, and any other important issues.



ANNEX C
Page 7 of 71
LATVIA MUNICIPAL SERVICES DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
Riga Urban Transport Component
Terms of Reference for the Riga Municipality Public Transport Unit
1.    Riga Municipality will have a key role in creating the appropriate institutional framework for
the transition to a market-led public transport sector in Riga. It will be important for the development
of the city's public transport service that local elected deputies are seen to be fully accountable for the
coordination and monitoring of service quality standards. The PTU will thus have to demonstrate
strong leadership and give clear direction to the operating enterprises in order to create confidence in
the local community.
2.     The overall strategic objectives of the PTU are as follows:
2.1    To design and secure the provision of a high quality, comprehensive, public transport
network, with appropriate time tabling which maximizes passenger benefits and
therefore maximizes patronage.
2.2    To ensure that resources and subsidies are effectively deployed across the network in
line with current and expected demand.
2.3    To ensure that subsidies provide good value for money, to be monitored by measuring
on-vehicle patronage.
2.4    To oversee the fares and ticketing systems to ensure that fraud is minimized.
2.5    To encourage the three public companies to produce constructive proposals to improve
the network and reduce the required subsidy levels.
2.6    To encourage operators to produce appropriate and sufficient publicity and
information to ensure that the use of services is maximized.
2.7    To administer and develop the vehicle and operator licensing system so that it can be
readily expanded to allow the introduction of more private operators.
2.7    To reduce the barriers to the entry of new operators so that healthy competition can
be encouraged.
3.    The detailed objectives of the PTU are stated below:
3.1    To monitor the operator's performance against agreed target measures (including
quality and safety standards) as defined in the schedules to the contracts between the
municipality and the enterprises.
3.2    To control the issue of operating licenses and their related inspection.



ANNEX C
Page 8 of 71
3.3    To ensure that market changes are determined by survey and analyzed, and that the
survey outputs are distributed to all operators to ensure maximum service provision.
3.4    To promote the development of traffic management schemes in the interest of
improving on-street operating conditions for all public modes of transport.
3.5    To design the route network.
3.6    To develop fares and subsidy policies.
3.7    To monitor contracts with the public transport enterprises.
3.8    To take responsibility for administering the ticketing system and the revenue control
inspectors.
4.     Riga City Council, in turn, should carry out the following basic tasks:
4.1    To oversee and monitor the development and implementation of the initial public
transport survey and resultant demand model which is to be carried out by the Danish
consultants RH&H in the second half of 1995.
4.2    To ensure that the model is updated and refined periodically as passenger demand
changes over time.
4.3   In conjunction with the main public transport operators, to design a public transport
network which specifies routes, service frequencies and a quality standard.
4.4    To consider the optimum balance between fare levels and the required subsidy.
4.5    To design and update the Riga concession fare policy, to monitor its use and to ensure
fair financial compensation among all operators.
4.6    To produce all public transport tickets and to distribute them to agents throughout
the city; to collect all off-vehicle revenue and to re-distribute revenues among
operators in proportion to passenger kilometres carried.
4.7    To take direct responsibility for the Riga-wide revenue control inspectors and charge
an appropriate penalty fare to act as a deterrent to fares evasion. Any such monies
raised will be retained by the public transport unit to offset the costs of the
inspectors.
4.8    To monitor the improving performance of the three Municipal Enterprises - TTP,
Imanta and Talava. These companies will remain in the ownership of Riga City
Council for a period of at least three years to allow the full benefits of the initiatives
proposed in the Business Plan to take effect before any possible privatisation.
4.9    To move towards the establishment of legal contracts between Riga City Council and



ANNEX C
Page 9 of 71
the three operating companies regarding levels of service, fares service quality and
subsidy for a period of one or more years. These contracts will initially cover all the
routes operated by each company, but will be capable of development over time to
introduce elements of competitive lendering among the three companies and any other
public transport operators.
4.10   To promote the public transport network by the provision of appropriate passenger
information at key points throughout the city.
4.11   To oversee the disbursement and monitor the effects of any funds or assets which may
be provided by the World Bank or any other development agency.
5.    In addition to the above-described, long term, broad responsibilities of the PTU, the unit will
also have the medium term responsibility of coordinating the execution of those elements of the
Municipal Services Development Project related to the Riga urban transport component. The PTU
will coordinate the aforementioned work throughout the duration of the project. The duties of the
PTU in this context will include:
5.1    Coordinate, on behalf of Riga City Council (RCC), the relations between RCC, the
World Bank, and any consultants and contractors appointed under the component.
5.2    Monitor the use of the World Bank loan.
5.3    On behalf of RCC, carry out the following tasks: prepare terms of reference and
letters of invitations for any consultancies to be carried out under the project; prepare
short-lists of consultants to be invited to submit proposals; prepare technical
specifications and associated bidding documents for the various bidding packages to be
carried out under the project; issue documentation to consultants and contractors,
respond to queries raised, and issue addenda as necessary; evaluate consultants
statements of capability and contractors prequalification documents; evaluate
consultants proposals and contractors bids and prepare evaluation reports; help RCC
with the negotiation and signing of the resulting contracts.
5.4    Coordinate the implementation of recommendations made in World Bank project
supervision reports.
5.5   Prepare semi-annual reports as outlined in Section V of the Project Implementation
Plan and submit to the Project Coordination Unit and to the World Bank.
5.6    Monitor project implementation and expenditure, and prepare and submit
disbursement requests, copies of which should be submitted to the World Bank, the
Project Coordination Unit, and the Ministry of Finance.
5.7    Monitor the training and technology and skill transfer programs to be provided under
the project's technical assistance.



ANNEX C
Page 10 of 71
5.8    Monitor all aspects of the Riga urban transport component of the project and prepare
written warnings about possible problems and delays as well as proposing technical,
financial and institutional measures necessary to improve project implementation.
5.9    Coordinate the execution of the different contracts to ensure overall work programs
are maintained.
5.10   Monitor and report on the execution of the Action Plans incorporated within the
Business Plans which have been elaborated and agreed upon for each of the operators.
5.11   Hold regular meetings with RCC to discuss project progress, the previous week's
work program, the coming week's work program, problems encountered, solutions
proposed, performance of consultants and contractors, and any other important issues.

LATVIA MUNICIPAL SERVICES DEVELOPMENT PROJECT
Municipal Development Fund Component
Terms of Reference for the Municipal Development Fund Administration
1.    The Municipal Development Fund (MDF) will be administered by the Public Investment
Program (PIP) in the Ministry of Economy under supervision of a Board of Directors. Additional
staff with expertise in financial and economic analysis and with civil engineering experience will be
required to supplement the present capacity of the PIP. The costs of these staff will be paid out of
the project and will be covered through an administrative mark-up on loan funds to be charged by the
Ministry of Finance.
2.    The main responsibilities of the PIP with regard to the MDF will be to:
2.1    Provide guidance and assistance to municipalities preparing proposals for submission
to the MDF;
2.2    Review proposals prepared by the municipalities for financing under the MDF in
accordance with agreed criteria and procedures;
2.3    Liaise with sector Ministries to review technical aspects of sub-project proposals;
2.4   Present proposals to the MDF Board of Directors for final decision;
2.5    Coordinate with the World Bank to obtain necessary approvals for first three MDF
sub-projects and for any sub-project over US$500,000;
2.6    Monitor progress of sub-projects funded under the MDF including status of financial
covenants;
2.7    Assist the Ministry of Finance with management of procurement and disbursement of
MDF sub-projects as necessary;
2.8   Prepare semi-annual reports, as described in the Project Implementation Plan, of MDF
performance for submission to the Board of Directors of the MDF, the Project
Coordination Unit (PCU) in the Ministry of Environment and Regional Development
and the World Bank;
2.9    Liaise with the PCU and World Bank and provide information on issues and problems
in sub-project implementation;
2.10   Ensure audit of MDF sub-projects as required.
2.11   Prepare an analysis of MDF performance for submission to the Bank during the
project's mid-term review. This analysis to include an estimation of financing needs of



ANNEX C
Page 12 of 71
the municipal sector, external financing requirements and recommendations as to
whether the program should be expanded to become a focal point for the channeling
of funds to the sector.
3.     For the individual sub-projects, the responsibilities of the PIP as a project management unit
will include the following:
3.1    Carry out the following tasks: prepare terms of reference and letters of invitations for
any consultancies to be carried out under the sub-projects; prepare short-lists of
consultants to be invited to submit proposals; prepare technical specifications and
associated bidding documents for the various bidding packages to be carried out under
the sub-projects; issue documentation to consultants and contractors, respond to
queries raised, and issue addenda as necessary; evaluate consultants statements of
capability and contractors prequalification documents; evaluate consultants proposals
and contractors bids and prepare evaluation reports; oversee negotiations and the
signing of the resulting contracts.
3.2    Coordinate the implementation of recommendations made in World Bank project
supervision reports.
3.3    Prepare semi-annual reports as outlined in Section V of the Project Implementation
Plan and submit to the Project Coordination Unit and to the World Bank.
3.4    Monitor project implementation and expenditure, and prepare and submit
disbursement requests, copies of which should be submitted to the World Bank and
the Ministry of Finance.
3.5    Monitor any training and technology and skill transfer programs to be provided under
the sub-project's technical assistance.
3.6    Monitor all aspects of the MDF component of the project and prepare written
warnings about possible problems and delays as well as proposing technical, financial
and institutional measures necessary to improve sub-project implementation.
3.7    Coordinate the execution of the different contracts to ensure overall work programs
are maintained.
3.8    Hold regular meetings with the Board of Directors to discuss sub-project progress,
sub-project work programs, problems encountered, solutions proposed, performance
of consultants and contractors, and any other important issues.

Terms of Reference
for
Project Coordination Unit
Municipal Services Development Project
Abbreviations:
MDF - Municipal Development Fund
MSDF - Municipal Services Development Project
MOERD - Ministry of Environmental Protection and Regional Development
PIP - Public Investment Program
PCU - Project Coordination Unit
PMU - Project Management Unit
TOR - Terms of Reference
Termiinology
Project - the Municipal Services Development Project
Project components - component of the Municipal Services Development Project -
Riga Urban Transport, Daugavpils Water and Wastewater, Municipal Development Fund
General
These Terms of Reference set out the tasks and services to be provided by the Project Coordination
Unit of the Municipal Services Development Project.
The PCU will provide the overall coordination of the Project. It will be located within the Ministry
of Environmental Protection and Regional Development. The PCU will monitor Project
implementation, coordinate procurement and track progress of disbursement and compliance with
Project conditionality; maintain relations with the World Bank, co-financiers, and donors and assist
them in the Project monitoring and supervision; provide general support to the PMUs for
procurement, disbursement, accounting, audit and reporting.
Management of each component of the MSDP would be the responsibility of the PMUs of each
component and the PIP for the sub-projects of the MDF component. So, the primary responsibility
for the Project implementation will be decentralized to local authorities, who should establish PMUs
for each of the sub-projects and the PIP unit. These units will be responsible for preparation of
designs, specifications, procurement, disbursement, construction supervision, institutional
strengthening, implementation of policy reforms required under the Project components, and reporting
and projects accounts. The PMUs and the PIP unit will be assisted by consultants with experience in
establishment of proper procedures including preparation of specifications and specific bid documents
based on the Bank's standard bidding documents.



ANNEX C
Page 14 of 71
Responsibilities of the PCU
Supervision of the Project components:
cooperate with the PMUs, municipalities and municipal enterprises in coordination and
supervision of civil works construction and equipment purchases under the Project and in
managing any consultant teams provided under the project;
monitor the Project progress, its implementation as compared to project implementation plans
including project milestones and timetables of each component and schedules:
review performance of participating entities with regard to financial and operational
covenants;
track the progress of procurement, disbursements, project accounting and auditing and
compliance of these with the Project conditionality
Communication with the World Bank, co-financiers, donors, and Ministries:
brief the Ministries, the World Bank, and the donor agencies officials on project performance
on a regular basis and alert them to existence of problems in implementation of the Project or
compliance with all covenants.
If the Steering Group is established, communicate with it, prepare its meetings;
liaise with local governments to resolve such problems soliciting assistance from the Ministry
and the World Bank as necessary;
maintain the communication between the Ministry of Environmental Protection and Regional
Development, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Transport, the PIP unit, the World Bank and
co-financiers as necessary
in cooperation with the PMUs and the PIP unit prepare semi-annual reports on Project status
including summary of project accounts for submission to the World Bank, central
government, co-financiers and donors.
Assistance to PMUs
provide general support to the PMUs for procurement, disbursement, accounting, audit and
reporting.
The PCU will assist the Projects Department in any other work, requested by the Department in
relation to the Project.



ANNEX C
Page 15 of 71
Staffing Requirements
The Project Coordination Unit will consist of experienced staff with civil engineering, financial and
environment, transport, and legal backgrounds.
The PCU will consist of:
two senior staff - the Unit Director and the Specialist. The Unit Director will be responsible
for the management of the work of the Unit. He or she must be familiar with issues like
supervision of civil works construction, review of project accounts, organization of
procurement and disbursement. He or she must posses excellent interpersonal skills. The
Director will be supported by the Specialist, who must be familiar with the same issues so
that the senior staff able to work in the following fields: engineering, finance, environment,
transport, legal issues.
one junior staff - the Unit Assistant. He or she should provide secretarial services to the
Unit, and keep the accounts of the Unit.
Each member of the PCU must be able to speak, read and write Latvian. Senior staff should possess
knowledge of English. Everybody must possess computer skills, be able to use Microsoft World and
Excel.

(I net positive effect)
Business Plan, additional revenue and reduced costs mainly due to:
(excluding fares increase & extra revenue from own funided investments)
- purchase of new vehicles and retirement of old vehicles.
Conversion of tram traction system (for TTP only).
50% reduction in fares evasion.
- Compersation for consessionary fares.
- Redefining network after survey.
Investment in spares and new plant & equipment.
Technical support and training.
Social tax is provided at 41% of payroll cost.
Base operaLing costs (Do nothing scenario):
Retained at 1995 level, except for:
Maintenanme & repair staff cost: increased by 2.5% (TTP) and 5% (ImantarTalava) each yew on previous year's cost.
Stores and materials cost: itcreased by 2.5% (TIP) and 7% (ImanLarTalava) each year on previous year's cost.
Depreciation cost: TTP - decreased by 5% each year on previous year's cost, starting 1996.
ImantaflTalava - round sum reductions to 1998; constant thereafter.
Depreciation:
Existing assets: as per present company rates.
New assets: Trams - 30 years.
Trolleybuses - 15 years.
Buses - 12 years.
Corporate tax:
Tax rate: 25%
Capital allowance: 40%
(- Capital allowance on written down value of fixed assets, including new investments.)
Unutilized tax losses, including available capital allowances, are carried forward
for five years, for set off against future profits.
